<p><b>Catherine of Aragon</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es" xml:lang="es"><i>Catalina de Aragón</i></span>), <a href="#Spelling_of_her_name">also spelled</a> <b>Katherine</b>, (16 December 1485 – 7 January 1536) was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_consorts" title="List of English consorts">Queen of England</a> from June 1509 until May 1533 as the <a href="/wiki/Wives_of_Henry_VIII" title="Wives of Henry VIII">first wife</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Henry_VIII" title="King Henry VIII">King Henry VIII</a>; she was previously <a href="/wiki/Princess_of_Wales" title="Princess of Wales">Princess of Wales</a> as the wife of Henry's elder brother <a href="/wiki/Arthur,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Arthur, Prince of Wales">Arthur</a>.</p>
<p>The daughter of <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Isabella I of Castile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">Ferdinand II of Aragon</a>, Catherine was three years old when she was betrothed to <a href="/wiki/Arthur,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Arthur, Prince of Wales">Arthur, Prince of Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heir_apparent" title="Heir apparent">heir apparent</a> to the English throne. They married in 1501, but Arthur died five months later on 2 April 1502. In 1507, she held the position of ambassadress for the Aragonese Crown in England, becoming the first female ambassador in European history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir199159_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir199159-1">[1]</a></sup> Catherine subsequently married Arthur's younger brother, the recently ascended Henry VIII, in 1509. For six months in 1513, she served as <a href="/wiki/Regent" title="Regent">regent</a> of England while Henry VIII was in France. During that time the English won the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Flodden" title="Battle of Flodden">Battle of Flodden</a>, an event in which Catherine played an important part with an emotional speech about English courage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECatherine_of_Aragon.2C_Queen_of_England_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECatherine_of_Aragon.2C_Queen_of_England-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 1525, Henry VIII was infatuated with <a href="/wiki/Anne_Boleyn" title="Anne Boleyn">Anne Boleyn</a> and dissatisfied that his marriage to Catherine had produced no surviving sons, leaving their daughter, the future <a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">Mary I of England</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Heir_presumptive" title="Heir presumptive">heir presumptive</a> at a time when there was no established precedent for a woman on the throne. He sought to have their marriage <a href="/wiki/Annulment" title="Annulment">annulled</a>, setting in motion a chain of events that led to England's schism with the Catholic Church. When <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_VII" title="Pope Clement VII">Pope Clement VII</a> refused to annul the marriage, Henry defied him by <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Supremacy" title="Acts of Supremacy">assuming supremacy</a> over religious matters. In 1533 their marriage was consequently declared invalid and Henry married Anne on the judgement of clergy in England, without reference to the Pope. Catherine refused to accept Henry as Supreme Head of the Church in England and considered herself the King's rightful wife and queen, attracting much popular sympathy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECatherine_of_Aragon_.281485.E2.80.931536.29_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECatherine_of_Aragon_.281485.E2.80.931536.29-3">[3]</a></sup> Despite this, she was acknowledged only as Dowager Princess of Wales by Henry. After being banished from court, she lived out the remainder of her life at <a href="/wiki/Kimbolton_Castle" title="Kimbolton Castle">Kimbolton Castle</a>, and died there on 7 January 1536. Catherine's English subjects held her in high esteem, and her death set off tremendous mourning among the English people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011295_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011295-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The controversial book <i>The Education of Christian Women</i> by <a href="/wiki/Juan_Luis_Vives" title="Juan Luis Vives">Juan Luis Vives</a>, which claimed women have the right to an education, was commissioned by and dedicated to her. Such was Catherine's impression on people that even her enemy, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cromwell" title="Thomas Cromwell">Thomas Cromwell</a>, said of her, "If not for her sex, she could have defied all the heroes of History."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChapuys1533737_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChapuys1533737-5">[5]</a></sup> She successfully appealed for the lives of the rebels involved in the <a href="/wiki/Evil_May_Day" title="Evil May Day">Evil May Day</a>, for the sake of their families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher_.26_Bietenholz1987283_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher_.26_Bietenholz1987283-6">[6]</a></sup> Catherine also won widespread admiration by starting an extensive programme for the relief of the poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECatherine_of_Aragon_Biography_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECatherine_of_Aragon_Biography-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher_.26_Bietenholz1987283_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher_.26_Bietenholz1987283-6">[6]</a></sup> She was a patron of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_humanism" title="Renaissance humanism">Renaissance humanism</a>, and a friend of the great scholars <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Erasmus_of_Rotterdam" title="Erasmus of Rotterdam">Erasmus of Rotterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_More" title="Thomas More">Thomas More</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECatherine_of_Aragon_Biography_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECatherine_of_Aragon_Biography-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Juan_de_Flandes_002.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2303" data-file-width="1576" height="321" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Juan_de_Flandes_002.jpg/220px-Juan_de_Flandes_002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Juan_de_Flandes_002.jpg/330px-Juan_de_Flandes_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Juan_de_Flandes_002.jpg/440px-Juan_de_Flandes_002.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Juan_de_Flandes_002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait by <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Flandes" title="Juan de Flandes">Juan de Flandes</a> thought to be of 11-year-old Catherine. She resembles her sister <a href="/wiki/Joanna_of_Castile" title="Joanna of Castile">Joanna of Castile</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Catherine was born at the Archbishop's Palace in <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares" title="Alcalá de Henares">Alcalá de Henares</a> near Madrid, on the night of 16 December 1485. She was the youngest surviving child of King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">Ferdinand II of Aragon</a> and Queen <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Isabella I of Castile</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011283_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011283-8">[8]</a></sup> Catherine was quite short in stature<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser199224_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser199224-9">[9]</a></sup> with long red hair, wide blue eyes, a round face, and a fair complexion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir199115_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir199115-10">[10]</a></sup> She was descended, on her maternal side, from the English royal house; her great-grandmother <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Lancaster" title="Catherine of Lancaster">Catherine of Lancaster</a>, after whom she was named, and her great-great-grandmother <a href="/wiki/Philippa_of_Lancaster" title="Philippa of Lancaster">Philippa of Lancaster</a> were both daughters of <a href="/wiki/John_of_Gaunt" title="John of Gaunt">John of Gaunt</a> and granddaughters of <a href="/wiki/Edward_III_of_England" title="Edward III of England">Edward III of England</a>. Consequently, she was third cousin of her father-in-law, <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011284_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011284-11">[11]</a></sup> and fourth cousin of her mother-in-law <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_York" title="Elizabeth of York">Elizabeth of York</a>.</p>
<p>Catherine was educated by a tutor, <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Geraldini" title="Alessandro Geraldini">Alessandro Geraldini</a>, who was a clerk in Holy Orders. She studied arithmetic, canon and civil law, classical literature, genealogy and heraldry, history, philosophy, religion, and theology. She had a strong religious upbringing and developed her Roman Catholic faith that would play a major role in later life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser199212_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser199212-12">[12]</a></sup> She learned to speak, read and write in Spanish and Latin, and spoke French and Greek. She was also taught domestic skills, such as cooking, dancing, drawing, embroidery, good manners, lace-making, music, needlepoint, sewing, spinning, and weaving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir199120_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir199120-13">[13]</a></sup> The great scholar <a href="/wiki/Erasmus" title="Erasmus">Erasmus</a> later said that Catherine "loved good literature which she had studied with success since childhood".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDowling198617_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDowling198617-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>At an early age, Catherine was considered a suitable wife for <a href="/wiki/Arthur,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Arthur, Prince of Wales">Arthur, Prince of Wales</a>, heir apparent to the English throne, due to the English ancestry she inherited from her mother. By means of her mother, Catherine had a stronger legitimate claim to the English throne than King Henry VII himself through the first two wives of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_of_Gaunt,_1st_Duke_of_Lancaster" title="John of Gaunt, 1st Duke of Lancaster">John of Gaunt, 1st Duke of Lancaster</a>: <a href="/wiki/Blanche_of_Lancaster" title="Blanche of Lancaster">Blanche of Lancaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Constance_of_Castile,_Duchess_of_Lancaster" title="Constance of Castile, Duchess of Lancaster">Constance of Castile</a>. In contrast, Henry VII was the descendant of Gaunt's third marriage to <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Swynford" title="Katherine Swynford">Katherine Swynford</a>, whose children were born out of wedlock and only legitimised after the death of Constance and the marriage of John to Katherine. The children of John and Katherine, while legitimised, were barred from inheriting the English throne, a stricture that was ignored in later generations. Because of Henry's descent through illegitimate children barred from succession to the English throne, the Tudor monarchy was not accepted by all European kingdoms. At the time, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Trast%C3%A1mara" title="House of Trastámara">House of Trastámara</a> was the most prestigious in Europe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011284_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011284-11">[11]</a></sup> due to the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a>, so the alliance of Catherine and Arthur validated the House of Tudor in the eyes of European royalty and strengthened the Tudor claim to the English throne via Catherine of Aragon's ancestry. It would have given a male heir an indisputable claim to the throne. The two were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Married_by_proxy" title="Married by proxy">married by proxy</a> on 19 May 1499 and corresponded in Latin until Arthur turned fifteen, when it was decided that they were old enough to be married.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESanders_.26_Low1910235_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESanders_.26_Low1910235-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Catherine of Aragon travelled to London, she brought a group of her African attendants with her, including one identified as the trumpeter <a href="/wiki/John_Blanke" title="John Blanke">John Blanke</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohn_Blanke_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohn_Blanke-16">[16]</a></sup> They are the first Africans recorded to have arrived in London at the time, and were considered luxury servants. They caused a great impression about the princess and the power of her family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2008166_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2008166-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="As_wife_and_widow_of_Arthur">As wife and widow of Arthur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: As wife and widow of Arthur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michel_Sittow_002.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="357" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Michel_Sittow_002.jpg/220px-Michel_Sittow_002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Michel_Sittow_002.jpg/330px-Michel_Sittow_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b0/Michel_Sittow_002.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michel_Sittow_002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait of a princess, possibly Catherine of Aragon, circa 1502, by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Sittow" title="Michael Sittow">Michael Sittow</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kunsthistorisches_Museum" title="Kunsthistorisches Museum">Kunsthistorisches Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The couple met on 4 November 1501 at <a href="/wiki/Dogmersfield" title="Dogmersfield">Dogmersfield</a> in Hampshire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStarkey200345.E2.80.9346_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStarkey200345.E2.80.9346-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETremlett201073_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETremlett201073-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECahill_Marr.C3.B3n2012_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECahill_Marr.C3.B3n2012-22">[22]</a></sup> Little is known about their first impressions of each other, but Arthur did write to his parents-in-law that he would be "a true and loving husband" and told his parents that he was immensely happy to "behold the face of his lovely bride". The couple had corresponded in Latin, but found that they could not understand each other, since they had learned different pronunciations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser199225_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser199225-23">[23]</a></sup> Ten days later, on 14 November 1501, they were married at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_St._Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="Old St. Paul's Cathedral">Old St. Paul's Cathedral</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011284_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011284-11">[11]</a></sup> A dowry of 200,000 crowns had been agreed, and half was paid shortly after the marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Once married, Arthur was sent to <a href="/wiki/Ludlow_Castle" title="Ludlow Castle">Ludlow Castle</a> on the borders of Wales to preside over the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Wales_and_the_Marches" title="Council of Wales and the Marches">Council of Wales and the Marches</a>, as was his duty as Prince of Wales, and his bride accompanied him. The couple stayed at <a href="/wiki/Castle_Lodge,_Ludlow" title="Castle Lodge, Ludlow">Castle Lodge, Ludlow</a>. A few months later, they both became ill, possibly with the <a href="/wiki/Sweating_sickness" title="Sweating sickness">sweating sickness</a> which was sweeping the area. Arthur died on 2 April 1502; Catherine recovered to find herself a widow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011285_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011285-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>At this point, Henry VII faced the challenge of avoiding the obligation to return her 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Ducat" title="Ducat">ducat</a> dowry, half of which he had not yet received, to her father, as required by her marriage contract should she return home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Following the death of his queen, Elizabeth of York, in February 1503, Henry VII initially considered marrying Catherine himself, but the opposition of her father and potential questions over the legitimacy of the couple's issue ended the idea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> To settle the matter, it was agreed that Catherine would marry Henry VII's second son, Henry, Duke of York, who was five years younger than she was. The death of Catherine's mother, however, meant that her "value" in the marriage market decreased. Castile was a much larger kingdom than Aragon, and it was inherited by Catherine's mentally unstable elder sister, <a href="/wiki/Joanna_of_Castile" title="Joanna of Castile">Joanna</a>. Ostensibly, the marriage was delayed until Henry was old enough, but Ferdinand II procrastinated so much over payment of the remainder of Catherine's dowry that it became doubtful that the marriage would take place. She lived as a virtual prisoner at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Durham_House_(London)" title="Durham House (London)">Durham House</a> in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams197115_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams197115-28">[28]</a></sup> Some of the letters she wrote to her father complaining of her treatment have survived. In one of these letters she tells him that "I choose what I believe, and say nothing. For I am not as simple as I may seem." She had little money and struggled to cope, as she had to support her ladies-in-waiting as well as herself. In 1507 she served as the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Ambassador" title="Ambassador">ambassador</a> to England, the first female ambassador in European history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir199159_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir199159-1">[1]</a></sup> While Henry VII and his councillors expected her to be easily manipulated, Catherine went on to prove them wrong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir199159_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir199159-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Marriage to Arthur's brother depended on the Pope granting a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papal_dispensation" title="Papal dispensation">dispensation</a> because <a href="/wiki/Canon_law" title="Canon law">canon law</a> forbade a man to <a href="/wiki/Affinity_(canon_law)" title="Affinity (canon law)">marry his brother's widow</a> (Lev. 18:16<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>). Catherine testified that her marriage to Arthur was never <a href="/wiki/Consummation" title="Consummation">consummated</a> as, also according to canon law, a marriage was not valid until consummated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir199134_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir199134-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011290_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011290-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Queen_of_England_.281509.E2.80.931533.29">Queen of England (1509–1533)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Queen of England (1509–1533)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Henry_VIII_Catherine_of_Aragon_coronation_woodcut.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="349" data-file-width="525" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Henry_VIII_Catherine_of_Aragon_coronation_woodcut.jpg/220px-Henry_VIII_Catherine_of_Aragon_coronation_woodcut.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Henry_VIII_Catherine_of_Aragon_coronation_woodcut.jpg/330px-Henry_VIII_Catherine_of_Aragon_coronation_woodcut.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Henry_VIII_Catherine_of_Aragon_coronation_woodcut.jpg/440px-Henry_VIII_Catherine_of_Aragon_coronation_woodcut.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Henry_VIII_Catherine_of_Aragon_coronation_woodcut.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
16th century woodcut of the <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">coronation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII of England</a> and Catherine of Aragon showing their heraldic badges, the Tudor Rose and the Pomegranate of Granada</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wedding">Wedding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Wedding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Catherine's wedding took place on 11 June 1509,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011287_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011287-32">[32]</a></sup> seven years after Prince Arthur's death. She married <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a>, who had only just acceded to the throne, in a private ceremony in the church of the Observant Friars outside Greenwich Palace. She was 23 years of age. The king was just days short of his 18th birthday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEagles2002194_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEagles2002194-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011287_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011287-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coronation">Coronation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Coronation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On Saturday 23 June 1509, the traditional eve-of-coronation procession to Westminster was greeted by a large and enthusiastic crowd. As was the custom, the couple spent the night before their <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">coronation</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a>. On Midsummer's Day, Sunday, <span class="nowrap">24 June</span> 1509, Henry VIII and Catherine were <a href="/wiki/Anointing" title="Anointing">anointed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">crowned</a> together by the Archbishop of Canterbury at a lavish ceremony at <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>. The coronation was followed by a banquet in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westminster_Hall" title="Westminster Hall">Westminster Hall</a>. Many new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knights_of_the_Bath" title="Knights of the Bath">Knights of the Bath</a> were created in honour of the coronation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011287_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011287-32">[32]</a></sup> In that month that followed, many social occasions presented the new Queen to the English public. She made a fine impression and was well received by the people of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011285_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011285-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pregnancies_and_children">Pregnancies and children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pregnancies and children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catharineofaragonengland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="201" data-file-width="600" height="74" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Catharineofaragonengland.jpg/220px-Catharineofaragonengland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Catharineofaragonengland.jpg/330px-Catharineofaragonengland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Catharineofaragonengland.jpg/440px-Catharineofaragonengland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catharineofaragonengland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Catherine watching Henry jousting in her honour after giving birth to a son. Henry's horse mantle is emblazoned with Catherine's initial letter, 'K.'</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Catherine was pregnant six times altogether:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011288_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011288-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>In August 1509, two months after the wedding, Catherine's first pregnancy was announced. On 31 January 1510 she gave birth prematurely to a stillborn girl.</li>
<li>In May 1510, four months after the loss of her first child, Catherine announced her second pregnancy. A son, <a href="/wiki/Henry,_Duke_of_Cornwall" title="Henry, Duke of Cornwall">Henry, Duke of Cornwall</a>, was born on 1 January 1511. In his honour, guns were fired from the Tower of London and the city bells were rung, beacons were lit and free wine was distributed to all the population. Five days after his birth, on 6 January 1511, the prince was christened at Richmond Palace, his godparents being the Archbishop of Canterbury, the Earl of Surrey and the Countess of Devon. On 22 February 1511, after only 52 days of life, the young prince died suddenly. It was said that he died of an intestinal complaint.</li>
<li>By early 1513, Catherine was pregnant again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERymer174148_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERymer174148-36">[36]</a></sup> On 30 June 1513, Catherine was left as regent in England when Henry VIII went to fight in France. In November 1513, she went into labour prematurely and gave birth to a stillborn boy.</li>
<li>In June 1514, Catherine announced her fourth pregnancy. On 8 January 1515, she gave birth to another stillborn boy.</li>
<li>In the summer of 1515, Catherine announced her fifth pregnancy; however, less hope was placed on an heir following her previous failed pregnancies. On 18 February 1516, Catherine delivered a healthy girl at 4 a.m. at Greenwich Palace, Kent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEagles2002195_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEagles2002195-37">[37]</a></sup> She was named <a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">Mary</a> and christened three days later (21 February) with great ceremony at the Church of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franciscan" title="Franciscan">Observant Friars</a>. Despite his evident disappointment, Henry VIII said that if it were a girl this time then surely boys would follow.</li>
<li>In February 1518, Catherine announced her sixth pregnancy. In March, she visited Merton College, Oxford and also made a pilgrimage to the shrine of St Frideswide, asking for a healthy son. On 10 November 1518 she gave birth to a daughter, but the child was weak and lived either only a few hours or at most a week.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence">Influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hans_Holbein_d._J._-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_-_WGA11564.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="975" data-file-width="816" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Hans_Holbein_d._J._-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_-_WGA11564.jpg/220px-Hans_Holbein_d._J._-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_-_WGA11564.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Hans_Holbein_d._J._-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_-_WGA11564.jpg/330px-Hans_Holbein_d._J._-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_-_WGA11564.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Hans_Holbein_d._J._-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_-_WGA11564.jpg/440px-Hans_Holbein_d._J._-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_-_WGA11564.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hans_Holbein_d._J._-_Portrait_of_Henry_VIII_-_WGA11564.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait of Henry VIII by <a href="/wiki/Hans_Holbein_the_Younger" title="Hans Holbein the Younger">Hans Holbein the Younger</a> circa 1540</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 11<span class="nowrap"> </span>June 1513, Henry appointed Catherine Regent or Governor of England while he went to France on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guinegate_(1513)" title="Battle of Guinegate (1513)">military campaign</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Louis_I_d%27Orl%C3%A9ans,_duc_de_Longueville" title="Louis I d'Orléans, duc de Longueville">Louis d'Orléans, Duke of Longueville</a>, was captured at <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9rouanne" title="Thérouanne">Thérouanne</a>, Henry sent him to stay in Catherine's household. She wrote to Wolsey that she and her council would prefer the Duke to stay in the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a> as the Scots were "so busy as they now be" and she added her prayers for "God to sende us as good lukke against the Scotts, as the King hath ther."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEllis1846152.E2.80.93154_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEllis1846152.E2.80.93154-39">[39]</a></sup> The war with Scotland occupied her subjects, and she was "horrible busy with making standards, banners, and badges" at <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Palace" title="Richmond Palace">Richmond Palace</a>. The Scots invaded and on 3 September 1513, she ordered <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lovell" title="Thomas Lovell">Thomas Lovell</a> to raise an army in the midland counties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERymer174149_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERymer174149-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Catherine rode north in full armour to address the troops, despite being heavily pregnant at the time. Her fine speech was reported to the historian <a href="/wiki/Peter_Martyr_d%27Anghiera" title="Peter Martyr d'Anghiera">Peter Martyr d'Anghiera</a> in <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a> within a fortnight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Although an Italian newsletter said she was 100 miles (160 km) north of London when news of the victory at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Flodden_Field" title="Battle of Flodden Field">Battle of Flodden Field</a> reached her, she was near <a href="/wiki/Buckingham" title="Buckingham">Buckingham</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> From <a href="/wiki/Woburn_Abbey" title="Woburn Abbey">Woburn Abbey</a> she sent a letter to Henry along with a piece of the bloodied coat of King <a href="/wiki/James_IV_of_Scotland" title="James IV of Scotland">James IV of Scotland</a>, who died in the battle, for Henry to use as a banner at the siege of <a href="/wiki/Tournai" title="Tournai">Tournai</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEllis184682.E2.80.9384.2C_88.E2.80.9389_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEllis184682.E2.80.9384.2C_88.E2.80.9389-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Catherine's religious dedication increased as she became older, as did her interest in academics. She continued to broaden her knowledge and provide training for her daughter, Mary. Education among women became fashionable, partly because of Catherine's influence, and she donated large sums of money to several colleges. Henry, however, still considered a male heir essential. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tudor_dynasty" title="Tudor dynasty">Tudor dynasty</a> was new, and its legitimacy might still be tested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011288.E2.80.93289_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011288.E2.80.93289-44">[44]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Anarchy" title="The Anarchy">A long civil war</a> (1135–54) had been fought the last time a woman, (<a href="/wiki/Empress_Matilda" title="Empress Matilda">Empress Matilda</a>), had inherited the throne. The disasters of civil war were still fresh in living memory from the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilkinson200970_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilkinson200970-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1520, Catherine's nephew <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011291_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011291-46">[46]</a></sup> paid a state visit to England, and she urged Henry to enter an alliance with Charles rather than with France. Immediately after his departure, she accompanied Henry to France on the celebrated visit to <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I</a>, the so-called <a href="/wiki/Field_of_the_Cloth_of_Gold" title="Field of the Cloth of Gold">Field of the Cloth of Gold</a>. Within two years, war was declared against France and the Emperor was once again welcome in England, where plans were afoot to betroth him to Catherine's daughter Mary.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_King.27s_great_matter">The King's great matter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The King's great matter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table border="0" cellpadding="2" cellspacing="2" style="float:right; margin:0 0 1em 1em; border:1px solid #aaa; background:#f9f9f9; text-align:left;">

Henry VIII</a></th>
</tr>

<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour,_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg"><img alt="Hans Holbein the Younger - Jane Seymour, Queen of England - Google Art Project.jpg" data-file-height="6824" data-file-width="4241" height="64" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/40px-Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/60px-Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/80px-Hans_Holbein_the_Younger_-_Jane_Seymour%2C_Queen_of_England_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" width="40"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Jane_Seymour" title="Jane Seymour">Jane Seymour</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AnneCleves.jpg"><img alt="AnneCleves.jpg" data-file-height="1106" data-file-width="829" height="53" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/AnneCleves.jpg/40px-AnneCleves.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/AnneCleves.jpg/60px-AnneCleves.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/AnneCleves.jpg/80px-AnneCleves.jpg 2x" width="40"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Cleves" title="Anne of Cleves">Anne of Cleves</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HowardCatherine02.jpeg"><img alt="HowardCatherine02.jpeg" data-file-height="255" data-file-width="205" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/HowardCatherine02.jpeg/40px-HowardCatherine02.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/HowardCatherine02.jpeg/60px-HowardCatherine02.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/HowardCatherine02.jpeg/80px-HowardCatherine02.jpeg 2x" width="40"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Howard" title="Catherine Howard">Catherine Howard</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Parr_from_NPG.jpg"><img alt="Catherine Parr from NPG.jpg" data-file-height="3042" data-file-width="2400" height="51" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Catherine_Parr_from_NPG.jpg/40px-Catherine_Parr_from_NPG.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Catherine_Parr_from_NPG.jpg/60px-Catherine_Parr_from_NPG.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Catherine_Parr_from_NPG.jpg/80px-Catherine_Parr_from_NPG.jpg 2x" width="40"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Parr" title="Catherine Parr">Catherine Parr</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Aragon_Henri_VIII_by_Henry_Nelson_ONeil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1795" data-file-width="2302" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Catherine_Aragon_Henri_VIII_by_Henry_Nelson_ONeil.jpg/220px-Catherine_Aragon_Henri_VIII_by_Henry_Nelson_ONeil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Catherine_Aragon_Henri_VIII_by_Henry_Nelson_ONeil.jpg/330px-Catherine_Aragon_Henri_VIII_by_Henry_Nelson_ONeil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Catherine_Aragon_Henri_VIII_by_Henry_Nelson_ONeil.jpg/440px-Catherine_Aragon_Henri_VIII_by_Henry_Nelson_ONeil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Aragon_Henri_VIII_by_Henry_Nelson_ONeil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The Trial of Queen Catherine of Aragon</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Nelson_O%27Neil" title="Henry Nelson O'Neil">Henry Nelson O'Neil</a> (1846–48, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Museum_and_Art_Gallery" title="Birmingham Museum and Art Gallery">Birmingham Museums</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1525, Henry VIII became enamoured of <a href="/wiki/Anne_Boleyn" title="Anne Boleyn">Anne Boleyn</a>, a lady-in-waiting to Queen Catherine who was 11 years younger than Henry. Henry began pursuing her;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEScarisbrick1997154_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScarisbrick1997154-47">[47]</a></sup> Catherine was no longer able to bear children by this time. Henry began to believe that his marriage was cursed and sought confirmation from the Bible, which he interpreted to say that if a man marries his brother's wife, the couple will be childless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECatherine_of_Aragon_Biography_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECatherine_of_Aragon_Biography-7">[7]</a></sup> Even if her marriage to Arthur had not been consummated (and Catherine would insist to her dying day that she had come to Henry's bed a virgin), Henry's interpretation of that biblical passage meant that their marriage had been wrong in the eyes of God.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011290_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011290-31">[31]</a></sup> Whether the Pope at the time of Henry and Catherine's marriage had had the right to overrule Henry's claimed scriptural impediment would become a hot topic in Henry's campaign to wrest an annulment from the present Pope.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011290_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011290-31">[31]</a></sup> It is possible that the idea of annulment had been suggested to Henry much earlier than this, and is highly probable that it was motivated by his desire for a son. Before Henry's father ascended the throne, England was beset by <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">civil warfare</a> over rival claims to the English crown, and Henry may have wanted to avoid a similar uncertainty over the succession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELacey197270_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELacey197270-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><i>My tribulations are so great, my life so disturbed by the plans daily invented to further the King's wicked intention, the surprises which the King gives me, with certain persons of his council, are so mortal, and my treatment is what God knows, that it is enough to shorten ten lives, much more mine.</i></p>
</blockquote>
<p>It soon became the one absorbing object of Henry's desires to secure an annulment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrigden2000114_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrigden2000114-50">[50]</a></sup> Catherine was defiant when it was suggested that she quietly retire to a nunnery, saying, "God never called me to a nunnery. I am the King's true and legitimate wife".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFarquhar200161_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFarquhar200161-51">[51]</a></sup> He set his hopes upon an appeal to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>, acting independently of Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wolsey" title="Thomas Wolsey">Thomas Wolsey</a>, whom he told nothing of his plans. <a href="/wiki/William_Knight_(bishop)" title="William Knight (bishop)">William Knight</a>, the King's secretary, was sent to <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_VII" title="Pope Clement VII">Pope Clement VII</a> to sue for an annulment, on the grounds that the dispensing <a href="/wiki/Papal_bull" title="Papal bull">bull</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Julius_II" title="Pope Julius II">Pope Julius II</a> was obtained by false pretences.</p>
<p>As the Pope was, at that time, the prisoner of Catherine's nephew, <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Charles V</a>, following the <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Rome_(1527)" title="Sack of Rome (1527)">Sack of Rome</a> in May 1527, Knight had difficulty in obtaining access to him. In the end, Henry's envoy had to return without accomplishing much. Henry now had no choice but to put this great matter into the hands of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wolsey" title="Thomas Wolsey">Thomas Wolsey</a>, and Wolsey did all he could to secure a decision in Henry's favour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cehen_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-cehen-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mary_I_by_Master_John.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3865" data-file-width="2924" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Mary_I_by_Master_John.jpg/220px-Mary_I_by_Master_John.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Mary_I_by_Master_John.jpg/330px-Mary_I_by_Master_John.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Mary_I_by_Master_John.jpg/440px-Mary_I_by_Master_John.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mary_I_by_Master_John.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Catherine and Henry's daughter <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">The Lady Mary</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Wolsey went so far as to convene an ecclesiastical court in England with a representative of the Pope presiding, and Henry and Catherine herself in attendance. The Pope had no intention of allowing a decision to be reached in England, and his legate was recalled. (How far the pope was influenced by Charles V is difficult to say, but it is clear Henry saw that the Pope was unlikely to annul his marriage to the Emperor's aunt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris1998166_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris1998166-53">[53]</a></sup>) The Pope forbade Henry to marry again before a decision was given in Rome. Wolsey had failed and was dismissed from public office in 1529. Wolsey then began a secret plot to have Anne Boleyn forced into exile and began communicating with the Pope to that end. When this was discovered, Henry ordered Wolsey's arrest and, had he not been <a href="/wiki/Terminal_illness" title="Terminal illness">terminally ill</a> and died in 1530, he might have been executed for <a href="/wiki/Treason" title="Treason">treason</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHaigh199392_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaigh199392-54">[54]</a></sup> A year later, Catherine was banished from court, and her old rooms were given to Anne Boleyn. When <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Warham" title="William Warham">William Warham</a> died, the Boleyn family's chaplain, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cranmer" title="Thomas Cranmer">Thomas Cranmer</a>, was appointed to the vacant position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cepop_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-cepop-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Henry decided to annul his marriage to Catherine, <a href="/wiki/John_Fisher" title="John Fisher">John Fisher</a> became her most trusted counsellor and one of her chief supporters. He appeared in the legates' court on her behalf, where he shocked people with the directness of his language, and by declaring that, like <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">John the Baptist</a>, he was ready to die on behalf of the indissolubility of marriage. Henry was so enraged by this that he wrote a long Latin address to the legates in answer to Fisher's speech. Fisher's copy of this still exists, with his manuscript annotations in the margin which show how little he feared Henry's anger. The removal of the cause to Rome ended Fisher's role in the matter, but Henry never forgave him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJestice2004277_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJestice2004277-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERex200327_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERex200327-57">[57]</a></sup> Other people who supported Catherine's case included <a href="/wiki/Thomas_More" title="Thomas More">Thomas More</a>, Henry's own sister <a href="/wiki/Mary_Tudor,_Queen_of_France" title="Mary Tudor, Queen of France">Mary Tudor, Queen of France</a>—though as a member of the Tudor family and of royal blood, she was safe from any punishment and execution—<a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_de_Salinas" title="María de Salinas">María de Salinas</a>, Holy Roman Emperor Charles V, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_III" title="Pope Paul III">Pope Paul III</a> and Protestant Reformers <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrecht199444_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrecht199444-58">[58]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/William_Tyndale" title="William Tyndale">William Tyndale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERees200677_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERees200677-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Banishment_and_death">Banishment and death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Banishment and death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
