</tr>
<tr>
<td>   <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Asturias" title="Isabella of Asturias">Isabella, Queen of Portugal</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>   <a href="/wiki/Joanna_of_Castile" title="Joanna of Castile">Joanna I, Queen of Aragon</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>   <a href="/wiki/John,_Prince_of_Asturias" title="John, Prince of Asturias">John, Prince of Asturias</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>   <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_of_Aragon_(1482-1517)" title="Maria of Aragon (1482-1517)">Mary, Queen of Portugal</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>   <strong class="selflink">Catherine, Queen of England</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="background:#ccccff; font-size: 100%; border-top: 1px solid #aaaaaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaaaaa; padding: 0 5px 0 5px;"><a href="/wiki/Joanna_of_Castile" title="Joanna of Castile">Joanna I</a></th>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Upon returning to <a href="/wiki/Dover" title="Dover">Dover</a> from a meeting with King <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I of France</a> in <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a>, Henry married Anne Boleyn in a secret ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011292_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011292-60">[60]</a></sup> Some sources speculate that Anne was already pregnant at the time (and Henry did not want to risk a son being born illegitimate) but others testify that Anne (who had seen her sister <a href="/wiki/Mary_Boleyn" title="Mary Boleyn">Mary Boleyn</a> taken up as the king's mistress and summarily cast aside) refused to sleep with Henry until they were married. Henry defended the legality of their union by pointing out that Catherine had previously been married. If she and Arthur had consummated their marriage, Henry by canon law had the right to remarry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStarkey2003462.E2.80.93464_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStarkey2003462.E2.80.93464-61">[61]</a></sup> On 23 May 1533, Cranmer, sitting in judgement at a special court convened at <a href="/wiki/Dunstable_Priory" title="Dunstable Priory">Dunstable Priory</a> to rule on the validity of Henry's marriage to Catherine, declared the marriage illegal, even though Catherine testified she and Arthur had never had physical relations. Cranmer ruled Henry and Anne's marriage valid five days later, on 28 May 1533.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams1971124_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams1971124-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Until the end of her life, Catherine would refer to herself as Henry's only lawful wedded wife and England's only rightful queen, and her servants continued to address her by that title. Henry refused her the right to any title but "<a href="/wiki/Dowager" title="Dowager">Dowager</a> Princess of Wales" in recognition of her position as his brother's widow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011292_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011292-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Catherine went to live at <a href="/wiki/The_More" title="The More">The More</a> castle in the winter of 1531/32.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011293_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011293-63">[63]</a></sup> In 1535 she was transferred to <a href="/wiki/Kimbolton_Castle" title="Kimbolton Castle">Kimbolton Castle</a>. There, she confined herself to one room (which she left only to attend Mass), dressed only in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hair_shirt" title="Hair shirt">hair shirt</a> of the Order of St. Francis, and fasted continuously. While she was permitted to receive occasional visitors, she was forbidden to see her daughter Mary. They were also forbidden to communicate in writing, but sympathizers discreetly ferried letters between the two. Henry offered both mother and daughter better quarters and permission to see each other if they would acknowledge Anne Boleyn as the new queen. Both refused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011293_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011293-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late December 1535, sensing her death was near, Catherine made her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Will_(law)" title="Will (law)">will</a>, and wrote to her nephew, the Emperor Charles V, asking him to protect her daughter. She then penned one final letter to Henry, her "most dear lord and husband":<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>My most dear lord, king and husband,</p>
<p>The hour of my death now drawing on, the tender love I owe you forceth me, my case being such, to commend myself to you, and to put you in remembrance with a few words of the health and safeguard of your soul which you ought to prefer before all worldly matters, and before the care and pampering of your body, for the which you have cast me into many calamities and yourself into many troubles. For my part, I pardon you everything, and I wish to devoutly pray God that He will pardon you also. For the rest, I commend unto you our daughter Mary, beseeching you to be a good father unto her, as I have heretofore desired. I entreat you also, on behalf of my maids, to give them marriage portions, which is not much, they being but three. For all my other servants I solicit the wages due them, and a year more, lest they be unprovided for. Lastly, I make this vow, that mine eyes desire you above all things.<br/>
Katharine the Quene.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Catherine died at <a href="/wiki/Kimbolton_Castle" title="Kimbolton Castle">Kimbolton Castle</a> on <span class="nowrap">7 January</span> 1536.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEagles2002202_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEagles2002202-65">[65]</a></sup> The following day, news of her death reached the king. At the time there were rumours that she was poisoned,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> possibly by <a href="/wiki/Gregory_di_Casale" title="Gregory di Casale">Gregory di Casale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> According to the chronicler <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hall" title="Edward Hall">Edward Hall</a>, Anne Boleyn wore yellow for the mourning, which has been interpreted in various ways; <a href="/wiki/Polydore_Vergil" title="Polydore Vergil">Polydore Vergil</a> interpreted this to mean that Anne did not mourn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarnicke1991187_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarnicke1991187-70">[70]</a></sup> Chapuys reported that it was King Henry who decked himself in yellow, celebrating the news and making a great show of his and Anne's daughter, Elizabeth, to his courtiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarnicke1991188_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarnicke1991188-71">[71]</a></sup> This was seen as distasteful and vulgar by many. Another theory is that the dressing in yellow was out of respect for Catherine as yellow was said to be the Spanish colour of mourning. Certainly, later in the day it is reported that Henry and Anne both individually and privately wept for her death. On the day of Catherine's funeral, Anne Boleyn <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">miscarried</a> a boy. Rumours then circulated that Catherine had been poisoned by Anne or Henry, or both, as Anne had threatened to murder both Catherine and Mary on several occasions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The rumours were born after the apparent discovery during her embalming that there was a black growth on her heart that might have been caused by poisoning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELofts1979139_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELofts1979139-72">[72]</a></sup> Modern medical experts are in agreement that her heart's discolouration was due not to poisoning, but to <a href="/wiki/Heart_cancer" title="Heart cancer">cancer</a>, something which was not understood at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011294_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011294-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Catherine was buried in <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_Cathedral" title="Peterborough Cathedral">Peterborough Cathedral</a> with the ceremony due to a Dowager <a href="/wiki/Princess_of_Wales" title="Princess of Wales">Princess of Wales</a>, not a queen. Henry did not attend the funeral and forbade Mary to attend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehman2011294_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehman2011294-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBietenholz_.26_Deutscher2003284_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBietenholz_.26_Deutscher2003284-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Faith">Faith</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Faith">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catherine_of_Aragon_as_Mary_Magdalene.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="678" data-file-width="530" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Catherine_of_Aragon_as_Mary_Magdalene.jpg/220px-Catherine_of_Aragon_as_Mary_Magdalene.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Catherine_of_Aragon_as_Mary_Magdalene.jpg/330px-Catherine_of_Aragon_as_Mary_Magdalene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Catherine_of_Aragon_as_Mary_Magdalene.jpg/440px-Catherine_of_Aragon_as_Mary_Magdalene.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catherine_of_Aragon_as_Mary_Magdalene.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Michael_Sittow" title="Michael Sittow">Michael Sittow</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Magdalene" title="Mary Magdalene">Mary Magdalene</a></i>, probably using Catherine as model</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Catherine was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Order_of_Saint_Francis" title="Third Order of Saint Francis">Third Order of Saint Francis</a> and she was punctilious in her religious obligations in the Order, integrating without demur her necessary duties as queen with her personal piety. After her divorce, she was quoted "I would rather be a poor beggar’s wife and be sure of heaven, than queen of all the world and stand in doubt thereof by reason of my own consent."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>The outward celebration of saints and holy <a href="/wiki/Relic" title="Relic">relics</a> formed no major part of her personal devotions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODNB_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-ODNB-76">[76]</a></sup> which she rather expressed in the <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Mass</a>, prayer, <a href="/wiki/Confession_(religion)" title="Confession (religion)">confession</a> and <a href="/wiki/Penance" title="Penance">penance</a>. Privately, however, she was aware of what she identified as the shortcomings of the papacy and church officialdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODNB_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-ODNB-76">[76]</a></sup> Her doubts about Church improprieties certainly did not extend so far as to support the allegations of corruption made public by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> in Wittenberg in 1517, which were soon to have such far-reaching consequences in initiating the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>.</p>
<p>In 1523 Alfonso de Villa Sancta, a learned <a href="/wiki/Friar" title="Friar">friar</a> of the Observant (reform) branch of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franciscan" title="Franciscan">Friars Minor</a> and friend of the king's old advisor <a href="/wiki/Erasmus" title="Erasmus">Erasmus</a>, dedicated to the queen his book <i>De Liberio Arbitrio adversus Melanchthonem</i> denouncing <a href="/wiki/Philip_Melanchthon" title="Philip Melanchthon">Philip Melanchthon</a>, a supporter of Luther. Acting as her <a href="/wiki/Confessor" title="Confessor">confessor</a>, he was able to nominate her for the title of "<a href="/wiki/Fidei_defensor" title="Fidei defensor">Defender of the Faith</a>" for denying Luther's arguments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser199295_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser199295-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearance">Appearance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Appearance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Catherine was of a very fair complexion, had blue eyes, and had a hair colour that was between <a href="/wiki/Red_hair" title="Red hair">reddish</a>-blonde and <a href="/wiki/Auburn_hair" title="Auburn hair">auburn</a> like her mother and sister Joanna.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In her youth she was described as "the most beautiful creature in the world"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir199181_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir199181-78">[78]</a></sup> and that there was "nothing lacking in her that the most beautiful girl should have."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser199224_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser199224-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_More" title="Thomas More">Thomas More</a> and Lord Herbert would reflect later in her lifetime that in regard to her appearance "there were few women who could compete with the Queen [Catherine] in her prime."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir1991104_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir1991104-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStrickland493_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStrickland493-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy.2C_memory.2C_and_historiography">Legacy, memory, and historiography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Legacy, memory, and historiography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares_-_Madrid_-_083.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="2112" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares_-_Madrid_-_083.jpg/220px-Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares_-_Madrid_-_083.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares_-_Madrid_-_083.jpg/330px-Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares_-_Madrid_-_083.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares_-_Madrid_-_083.jpg/440px-Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares_-_Madrid_-_083.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares_-_Madrid_-_083.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of Catherine at <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares" title="Alcalá de Henares">Alcalá de Henares</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The controversial book "The Education of Christian Women" by <a href="/wiki/Juan_Luis_Vives" title="Juan Luis Vives">Juan Luis Vives</a>, which claimed women have the right to an education, was dedicated to and commissioned by her. Such was Catherine's impression on people, that even her enemy, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cromwell" title="Thomas Cromwell">Thomas Cromwell</a>, said of her "If not for her sex, she could have defied all the heroes of History."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChapuys1533737_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChapuys1533737-5">[5]</a></sup> She successfully appealed for the lives of the rebels involved in the <a href="/wiki/Evil_May_Day" title="Evil May Day">Evil May Day</a> for the sake of their families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher_.26_Bietenholz1987283_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher_.26_Bietenholz1987283-6">[6]</a></sup> Furthermore, Catherine won widespread admiration by starting an extensive programme for the relief of the poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutscher_.26_Bietenholz1987283_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutscher_.26_Bietenholz1987283-6">[6]</a></sup> She was also a patron of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_humanism" title="Renaissance humanism">Renaissance humanism</a>, and a friend of the great scholars <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Erasmus_of_Rotterdam" title="Erasmus of Rotterdam">Erasmus of Rotterdam</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas_More" title="Saint Thomas More">Saint Thomas More</a>. Some saw her as a martyr.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the reign of her daughter <a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">Mary I of England</a>, her marriage to Henry VIII was declared "good and valid". Her daughter Queen Mary also had several portraits commissioned of Catherine, and it would not by any means be the last time she was painted. After her death, numerous portraits were painted of her, particularly of her speech at the Legatine Trial, a moment accurately rendered in Shakespeare's play about Henry VIII.</p>
<p>Her tomb in <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_Cathedral" title="Peterborough Cathedral">Peterborough Cathedral</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFroude1891389_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFroude1891389-83">[83]</a></sup> can be seen and there is hardly ever a time when it is not decorated with flowers or pomegranates, her heraldic symbol. It bears the title <i>Katharine Queen of England</i>.</p>
<p>In the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a>'s wife, <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Teck" title="Mary of Teck">Mary of Teck</a>, had her grave upgraded and there are now banners there denoting Catherine as a Queen of England. Every year at Peterborough Cathedral there is a service in her memory. There are processions, prayers, and various events in the Cathedral including processions to Catherine's grave in which candles, pomegranates, flowers and other offerings are placed on her grave. On the service commemorating the 470th anniversary of her death, the Spanish Ambassador to the United Kingdom attended. During the 2010 service a rendition of Catherine of Aragon's speech before the Legatine court was read by <a href="/wiki/Jane_Lapotaire" title="Jane Lapotaire">Jane Lapotaire</a>. There is a statue of her in her birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares" title="Alcalá de Henares">Alcalá de Henares</a>, as a young woman holding a book and a rose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Catherine has remained a popular biographical subject to the present day. The American historian <a href="/wiki/Garrett_Mattingly" title="Garrett Mattingly">Garrett Mattingly</a> was the author of a popular biography <i>Katherine of Aragon</i> in 1942. In 1966, Catherine and her many supporters at court were the subjects of <i>Catherine of Aragon and her Friends</i>, a biography by John E. Paul. In 1967, Mary M. Luke wrote the first book of her Tudor trilogy, <i>Catherine the Queen</i> which portrayed her and the controversial era of English history through which she lived.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peterborough_Katherine_of_Aragon.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="641" data-file-width="864" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Peterborough_Katherine_of_Aragon.JPG/220px-Peterborough_Katherine_of_Aragon.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Peterborough_Katherine_of_Aragon.JPG/330px-Peterborough_Katherine_of_Aragon.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Peterborough_Katherine_of_Aragon.JPG/440px-Peterborough_Katherine_of_Aragon.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peterborough_Katherine_of_Aragon.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Grave of Catherine of Aragon in <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_Cathedral" title="Peterborough Cathedral">Peterborough Cathedral</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In recent years, the historian <a href="/wiki/Alison_Weir" title="Alison Weir">Alison Weir</a> covered her life extensively in her biography <i><a href="/wiki/The_Six_Wives_of_Henry_VIII_(book)" title="The Six Wives of Henry VIII (book)">The Six Wives of Henry VIII</a></i>, first published in 1991. <a href="/wiki/Antonia_Fraser" title="Antonia Fraser">Antonia Fraser</a> did the same in her own 1992 biography of the same title; as did the British historian <a href="/wiki/David_Starkey" title="David Starkey">David Starkey</a> in his 2003 book <i>Six Wives: The Queens of Henry VIII</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStarkey20031_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStarkey20031-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir19911_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir19911-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser19921_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser19921-87">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Giles_Tremlett" title="Giles Tremlett">Giles Tremlett</a>'s biography <i>Catherine of Aragon: The Spanish Queen of Henry VIII</i> came out in 2010, and <a href="/wiki/Julia_Fox" title="Julia Fox">Julia Fox</a>'s 2011 dual biography <i>Sister Queens: The Noble, Tragic Lives of Katherine of Aragon and Juana, Queen of Castile</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_and_statues">Places and statues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Places and statues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares" title="Alcalá de Henares">Alcalá de Henares</a>, the place of Catherine's birth, a statue of Catherine as a young woman holding a rose and a book can be seen in the Archbishop's Palace.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peterborough" title="Peterborough">Peterborough</a> is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_twinning" title="Town twinning">twinned</a> with the Spanish city of Alcalá de Henares, located in the wider Community of Madrid. Children from schools in the two places have learned about each other as part of the twinning venture, and artists have even come over from Alcalá de Henares to paint Catherine's tombstone.</li>
<li>Many places in <a href="/wiki/Ampthill" title="Ampthill">Ampthill</a> are named after Catherine. Also in Ampthill there is a cross in Ampthill Great Park named "Queen Catherine's Cross" in her honour. It is on the site of the castle where she was sent during her divorce from the King.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spelling_of_her_name">Spelling of her name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Spelling of her name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Her baptismal name was "Catalina", but "Katherine" was soon the accepted form in England after her marriage to Arthur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODNB_76-2"><a href="#cite_note-ODNB-76">[76]</a></sup> Catherine herself signed her name "Katherine", "Katherina", "Katharine" and sometimes "Katharina". In a letter to her, Arthur, her husband, addressed her as "Princess Katerine". Her daughter Queen Mary I called her "Quene Kateryn", in her will. Rarely were names, particularly first names, written in an exact manner during the sixteenth century and it is evident from Catherine's own letters that she endorsed different variations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Loveknots built into his various palaces by her husband, Henry VIII, display the initials "H &amp; K",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> as do other items belonging to Henry and Catherine, including gold goblets, a gold salt cellar, basins of gold, and candlesticks. Her tomb in <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_Cathedral" title="Peterborough Cathedral">Peterborough Cathedral</a> is marked "Katharine Queen of England".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser199257.E2.80.9358_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser199257.E2.80.9358-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-findagrave_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-findagrave-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Catherine_of_Aragon.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1350" data-file-width="1550" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coat_of_Arms_of_Catherine_of_Aragon.svg/170px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Catherine_of_Aragon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coat_of_Arms_of_Catherine_of_Aragon.svg/255px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Catherine_of_Aragon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coat_of_Arms_of_Catherine_of_Aragon.svg/340px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Catherine_of_Aragon.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Catherine_of_Aragon.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Catherine of Aragon's arms while queen<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaclagan199927_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaclagan199927-92">[92]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_art_and_media">In art and media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: In art and media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Over the years, numerous artistic and cultural works have been dedicated to Catherine, have been written about her, or have mentioned her, including some by her husband <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a>, who wrote "Grene growth the holy"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> about and for her, and <a href="/wiki/Juan_Luis_Vives" title="Juan Luis Vives">Juan Luis Vives</a>, who dedicated <i>The Education of Christian Women</i> to her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir1991123_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir1991123-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Catherine of Aragon has been portrayed in film, television, plays, novels, songs, poems, and other creative forms many times, and as a result she has stayed very much in popular memory. There has never been a film or television series in which she is the main character, the nearest is the first episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Six_Wives_of_Henry_VIII_(BBC_TV_series)" title="The Six Wives of Henry VIII (BBC TV series)">The Six Wives of Henry VIII</a></i>, which is told from her point of view (and in which she is portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Annette_Crosbie" title="Annette Crosbie">Annette Crosbie</a>). <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>'s play <i><a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_(play)" title="Henry VIII (play)">Henry VIII</a></i> succeeds in recreating with great accuracy Catherine's statement about the legitimacy of her marriage at the court in Blackfriars before King Henry, and Shakespeare's portrayal of Catherine is remarkably sympathetic; however, most of the rest of the play is an attempt to absolve many, especially Henry VIII, and the timing of key incidents (including Catherine's death) is changed and other events are avoided (the play makes Henry nearly an innocent pawn in the hands of a dastardly Cardinal Wolsey, and the play stops short of Anne Boleyn's execution).</p>
<p>Although Catherine is often portrayed in film and on stage as having possessed stereotypically Spanish dark hair and eyes and olive complexion, existing portraits and contemporary descriptions depict her with blue eyes, fair skin, and reddish-blonde hair, not uncommon for Spaniards from the northern regions of Spain, including her father's land of <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a>. And she was part English, through her ancestresses <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Katherine_of_Lancaster" title="Katherine of Lancaster">Katherine of Lancaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philippa_of_Lancaster" title="Philippa of Lancaster">Philippa of Lancaster</a>, who were daughters of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_of_Gaunt,_1st_Duke_of_Lancaster" title="John of Gaunt, 1st Duke of Lancaster">John of Gaunt, 1st Duke of Lancaster</a>.</p>
<p>Catherine often is played with a Spanish accent. From most reports, this is accurate, as she never fully mastered the English language.</p>
<p>In January, 2013, the <a href="/wiki/National_Portrait_Gallery,_London" title="National Portrait Gallery, London">National Portrait Gallery</a> in London revealed that its curators had recently discovered that a portrait at <a href="/wiki/Lambeth_Palace" title="Lambeth Palace">Lambeth Palace</a> formerly believed to have been a portrait of Catherine Parr in fact shows Catherine of Aragon. The National Portrait Gallery announced that the painting, which had hung in a private sitting room of the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a> since at least the 19th century, would be paired with a portrait of Henry VIII already in the museum's collection, and would remain at the museum on loan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_rhymes">Music and rhymes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Music and rhymes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The song "Green groweth the holly" is said to have been written for her by Henry VIII.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir199178_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir199178-96">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the children's <a href="/wiki/Nursery_rhyme" title="Nursery rhyme">nursery rhyme</a> "<a href="/wiki/I_Had_a_Little_Nut_Tree" title="I Had a Little Nut Tree">I Had a Little Nut Tree</a>" she is the "King of Spain's Daughter."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorton195535_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorton195535-97">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Rick_Wakeman" title="Rick Wakeman">Rick Wakeman</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Six_Wives_of_Henry_VIII_(album)" title="The Six Wives of Henry VIII (album)">The Six Wives of Henry VIII</a></i>, "Catherine of Aragon" is listed as Track no. 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESigman2011135_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESigman2011135-98">[98]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Books">Books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dame_Ellen_Terry_as_Katherine_of_Aragon_Shakespeare_Henry_VIII.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="702" data-file-width="522" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Dame_Ellen_Terry_as_Katherine_of_Aragon_Shakespeare_Henry_VIII.jpg/220px-Dame_Ellen_Terry_as_Katherine_of_Aragon_Shakespeare_Henry_VIII.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Dame_Ellen_Terry_as_Katherine_of_Aragon_Shakespeare_Henry_VIII.jpg/330px-Dame_Ellen_Terry_as_Katherine_of_Aragon_Shakespeare_Henry_VIII.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Dame_Ellen_Terry_as_Katherine_of_Aragon_Shakespeare_Henry_VIII.jpg/440px-Dame_Ellen_Terry_as_Katherine_of_Aragon_Shakespeare_Henry_VIII.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dame_Ellen_Terry_as_Katherine_of_Aragon_Shakespeare_Henry_VIII.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dame <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Terry" title="Ellen Terry">Ellen Terry</a> as Catherine of Aragon</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Catherine is the main character in:</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Katharine, The Virgin Widow</i>, <i>The Shadow of the Pomegranate</i>, and <i>The King's Secret Matter</i> (later published in an omnibus <i>Katharine of Aragon</i>) by <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Hibbert" title="Eleanor Hibbert">Jean Plaidy</a></li>
<li><i>My Catalina</i> by <a href="/wiki/Maureen_Peters_(novelist)" title="Maureen Peters (novelist)">Maureen Peters</a></li>
<li><i>The King's Pleasure</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Norah_Lofts" title="Norah Lofts">Norah Lofts</a>;</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Constant_Princess" title="The Constant Princess">The Constant Princess</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Gregory" title="Philippa Gregory">Philippa Gregory</a> (a novel about Catherine's younger years);</li>
<li><i>Patience, Princess Catherine</i> by <a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Meyer" title="Carolyn Meyer">Carolyn Meyer</a> (young adult novel);</li>
<li><i>Isabella's Daughter</i> by Charity Bishop.</li>
<li><i>Catherine of Aragon/My Tudor Queen" by Alison Prince.</i></li>
<li><i>Katherine of Aragon, The True Queen</i> by <a href="/wiki/Alison_Weir" title="Alison Weir">Alison Weir</a></li>
<li>Falling Pomegranate Seeds: The Duty of Daughters (The Katherine of Aragon Story Book 1) <i>by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wendy_J._Dunn&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wendy J. Dunn (page does not exist)">Wendy J. Dunn</a></i></li>
<li>"Catherine of Aragon: An Intimate History of Henry VIII's True Wife" by Amy Licence.</li>
</ul>
<p>Catherine is a character in:</p>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Murder_Most_Royal" title="Murder Most Royal">Murder Most Royal</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Hibbert" title="Eleanor Hibbert">Jean Plaidy</a>;</li>
<li><i>The Trusted Servant</i> by Alison Macleod</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Other_Boleyn_Girl" title="The Other Boleyn Girl">The Other Boleyn Girl</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Gregory" title="Philippa Gregory">Philippa Gregory</a> (a novel about Mary Boleyn's life)</li>
<li><i>The Dark Rose</i>, Volume 2 of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Morland_Dynasty" title="The Morland Dynasty">The Morland Dynasty</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_Harrod-Eagles" title="Cynthia Harrod-Eagles">Cynthia Harrod-Eagles</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Wolf_Hall" title="Wolf Hall">Wolf Hall</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Hilary_Mantel" title="Hilary Mantel">Hilary Mantel</a></li>
<li><i>I, Elizabeth</i> by Rosalind Miles</li>
<li><i>Keeper of the King's Secrets</i> by Michelle Diener</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre.2C_film.2C_stage.2C_and_TV">Theatre, film, stage, and TV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_of_Aragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Theatre, film, stage, and TV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Catherine was portrayed by:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sarah_Siddons" title="Sarah Siddons">Sarah Siddons</a> in the 18th century, in Shakespeare's <i>Henry VIII</i>. She told <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Johnson" title="Samuel Johnson">Samuel Johnson</a> that the role of Queen Catherine was her favourite of all the Shakespearean roles she had played, as it was "the most natural".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Violet_Vanbrugh" title="Violet Vanbrugh">Violet Vanbrugh</a> in the 1911 short film production of <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>'s play <i><a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_(play)" title="Henry VIII (play)">Henry VIII</a></i> (first film portrayal).</li>
<li>German actress Hedwig Pauly-Winterstein in the film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anna_Boleyn" title="Anna Boleyn">Anna Boleyn</a></i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rosalie_Crutchley" title="Rosalie Crutchley">Rosalie Crutchley</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sword_and_the_Rose" title="The Sword and the Rose">The Sword and the Rose</a></i>, an account of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mary_Tudor_(queen_consort_of_France)" title="Mary Tudor (queen consort of France)">Mary Tudor</a>'s romance with the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Brandon,_1st_Duke_of_Suffolk" title="Charles Brandon, 1st Duke of Suffolk">Duke of Suffolk</a> in 1515. (Crutchley later played Henry's sixth queen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Katherine_Parr" title="Katherine Parr">Katherine Parr</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Six_Wives_of_Henry_VIII_(BBC_TV_series)" title="The Six Wives of Henry VIII (BBC TV series)">The Six Wives of Henry VIII</a></i>.)</li>
<li>Greek actress <a href="/wiki/Irene_Papas" title="Irene Papas">Irene Papas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hal_B._Wallis" title="Hal B. Wallis">Hal B. Wallis</a>' acclaimed film <i><a href="/wiki/Anne_of_the_Thousand_Days" title="Anne of the Thousand Days">Anne of the Thousand Days</a></i> (1969).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frances_Cuka" title="Frances Cuka">Frances Cuka</a> in the 1972 film <i><a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_and_His_Six_Wives" title="Henry VIII and His Six Wives">Henry VIII and His Six Wives</a></i>. Keith Michell reprised his role as Henry VIII. A scene was incorporated between Frances Cuka and <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Rampling" title="Charlotte Rampling">Charlotte Rampling</a> (playing Anne Boleyn) to show their quiet, glacial enmity.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Claire_Bloom" title="Claire Bloom">Claire Bloom</a> in a 1979 adaptation of Shakespeare's <i><a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_(play)" title="Henry VIII (play)">Henry VIII</a></i>.</li>
<li>British actress <a href="/wiki/Annette_Crosbie" title="Annette Crosbie">Annette Crosbie</a> in a 90-minute television drama titled <i>"Catherine of Aragon"</i>, the first part of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Six_Wives_of_Henry_VIII_(BBC_TV_series)" title="The Six Wives of Henry VIII (BBC TV series)">The Six Wives of Henry VIII</a></i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Annabelle_Dowler" title="Annabelle Dowler">Annabelle Dowler</a> in Dr. <a href="/wiki/David_Starkey" title="David Starkey">David Starkey</a>'s 2001 documentary series on Henry VIII's Six Wives.</li>
<li>Spanish actress <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yolanda_Vasquez" title="Yolanda Vasquez">Yolanda Vasquez</a>, a brief appearance in the British TV version <i>"<a href="/wiki/The_Other_Boleyn_Girl" title="The Other Boleyn Girl">The Other Boleyn Girl</a>"</i> (January 2003), opposite <a href="/wiki/Jared_Harris" title="Jared Harris">Jared Harris</a> as Henry VIII and <a href="/wiki/Natascha_McElhone" title="Natascha McElhone">Natascha McElhone</a> as <a href="/wiki/Mary_Boleyn" title="Mary Boleyn">Mary Boleyn</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Assumpta_Serna" title="Assumpta Serna">Assumpta Serna</a> in the October 2003 <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> two-part television drama, <i>"Henry VIII"</i> which starred <a href="/wiki/Ray_Winstone" title="Ray Winstone">Ray Winstone</a> in the title role. Part 1 chronicled the king's life from the birth of his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegitimacy" title="Illegitimacy">bastard</a> son, <a href="/wiki/Henry_FitzRoy,_1st_Duke_of_Richmond_and_Somerset" title="Henry FitzRoy, 1st Duke of Richmond and Somerset">Henry Fitzroy</a> until the execution of Anne Boleyn in 1536. <a href="/wiki/David_Suchet" title="David Suchet">David Suchet</a> co-starred as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_Wolsey" title="Cardinal Wolsey">Cardinal Wolsey</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marge_Simpson" title="Marge Simpson">Marge Simpson</a> (voiced by <a href="/wiki/Julie_Kavner" title="Julie Kavner">Julie Kavner</a>), as "Margerine of Aragon" in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Margical_History_Tour" title="Margical History Tour">Margical History Tour</a>."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maria_Doyle_Kennedy" title="Maria Doyle Kennedy">Maria Doyle Kennedy</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Showtime_(TV_network)" title="Showtime (TV network)">Showtime</a> 2007 television series, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tudors" title="The Tudors">The Tudors</a></i> opposite <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Rhys_Meyers" title="Jonathan Rhys Meyers">Jonathan Rhys Meyers</a> as Henry. For her performance, Kennedy won an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IFTA_Award" title="IFTA Award">IFTA Award</a> for Best Actress in a Supporting Role Television, and a Gemini Award for an Actress in a Featured Supporting Role in a Dramatic Series.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ana_Torrent" title="Ana Torrent">Ana Torrent</a> in the 2007 film adaptation of the novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Other_Boleyn_Girl" title="The Other Boleyn Girl">The Other Boleyn Girl</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Gregory" title="Philippa Gregory">Philippa Gregory</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Eric_Bana" title="Eric Bana">Eric Bana</a> as Henry VIII.</li>
<li>Virginia Weeks portrayed her in the play <i>Six Dead Queens and an Inflatable Henry</i>, and is one of only three productions that show Catherine with the correct colouring.</li>
<li>In 2008 she was played by Victoria Pelro in the film <i>The Twisted Tale of Bloody Mary</i>.</li>
<li>She is played by <a href="/wiki/Siobhan_Hewlett" title="Siobhan Hewlett">Siobhan Hewlett</a> in the 2009 documentary <i>Henry: Mind of a Tyrant</i>. This documentary is one of the few portrayals of Catherine to get her appearance correct.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kate_Duch%C3%AAne" title="Kate Duchêne">Kate Duchêne</a> in a 2010 adaptation of Shakespeare's <i><a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_(play)" title="Henry VIII (play)">Henry VIII</a></i> at <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare%27s_Globe" title="Shakespeare's Globe">Shakespeare's Globe</a> Theatre.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joanne_Whalley" title="Joanne Whalley">Joanne Whalley</a> in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wolf_Hall_(TV_series)" title="Wolf Hall (TV series)">Wolf Hall</a></i>.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Natalia_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Natalia Rodríguez Arroyo (page does not exist)">Natalia Rodríguez Arroyo</a> in the Spanish historical series <i><a href="/wiki/Isabel_(TV_series)" title="Isabel (TV series)">Isabel</a></i>.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=M%C3%A9lida_Molina&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mélida Molina (page does not exist)">Mélida Molina</a> in the Spanish historical series <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carlos,_Rey_Emperador" title="Carlos, Rey Emperador">Carlos, Rey Emperador</a></i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jessica_Ransom" title="Jessica Ransom">Jessica Ransom</a> in the CBBC series <a href="/wiki/Horrible_Histories_(2015_TV_series)" title="Horrible Histories (2015 TV series)">Horrible Histories</a></li>
</ul>
</div>

<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Catherine's endorsement of different spellings can be identified in numerous letters, signing herself as 'Katharine the Quene' in a letter to Wolsey in 1513 and as 'Katharine' in her final letter to Henry VIII dating to <span class="nowrap">Jan 1536</span>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-89">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As Latin inscriptions were used in structures, a "C" represented the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_numeral" title="Roman numeral">numeral 100</a>, so a "K" was used instead. The same was applied during the time of <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_France" title="Henry II of France">Henri II</a> and his wife <a href="/wiki/Catherine_de%27_Medici" title="Catherine de' Medici">Catherine</a> during her state entry in Paris on 18 June 1549.</span></li>
